المرصد الثالث - المقصد الثالث : في الكفر
العوام من ذلك . الذي ذكرتموه يقتضي أن يكون إيمان النبي وآحاد الأمة سواء وإنه باطل إجماعاً، ولقول أي ذلك الذي ذكرتموه ليس بصحيح لاقتضائه تلك المساواة، ولقول إبراهيم عليه السلام ولكن ليطمئن قلبي فإنه يدل على قبول التصديق اليقيني للزيادة كما سلف تقريره والظاهر أن الظن الغالب الذي لا يخطر معه احتمال النقيض بالبال حكمه حكم اليقين في كونه إيماناً حقيقياً فإن إيمان أكثر هذا القبيل، وعلى هذا فكون التصديق الإيماني قابلاً للزيادة واضح وضوحاً تاماً . الثاني : من وجهي التفاوت أعني ما هو بحسب المتعلق أن يقال : التصديق التفصيلي في أفراد ما علم مجيئه به جزء من الإيمان يثاب عليه ثوابه على تصديقه بالإجمال، يعني أن أفراد ما جاء به متعددة وداخلة في التصديق الإجمالي، فإذا علم واحد منها بخصوصه وصدق به كان هذا تصديقاً مغايراً لذلك التصديق المجمل وجزءاً من الإيمان، ولا شك أن التصديقات التفضلية تقبل الزيادة، فكذا الإيمان والنصوص كنحو قوله تعالى: ﴿ وإذا تليت عليهم آياته زادتهم إيماناً ﴾ دالة على قبوله لهما، أي قبول الإيمان للزيادة والنقصان بالوجه الثاني كما أن نص قوله : ولكن ليطمئن قلبي ﴾ دل على قبوله لهما بالوجه الأول .
قوله : ( ولا شك أن التصديقات التفصيلية إلخ) قيل : تلك التفاصيل لما كان الإيمان بها برمتها إجمالاً حاصلاً فبالاطلاع عليها لم ينقلب الإيمان من النقصان إلى الزيادة بل من الإجمال إلى التفصيل فقط، نعم يتصور ذلك التفاوت في عصر النبي عليه السلام فإن الإيمان لما كان عبارة عن التصديق بجملة ما جاء به النبي عليه السلام فكلما ازدادت تلك الجملة ازدادت تصديق المتعلق بها لا محالة .
قوله : (بالوجه الثاني) صرفه إلى قبوله لهما بالوجه الأول أيضاً، باعتبار هذه الدلالة، أعني دلالة قوله تعالى : وإذا تليت الآية غير مستبعد كما لا يخفى .
The third observation - the third objective: on disbelief. The common people from that. What you mentioned requires that the faith of the Prophet and the individuals of the community be equal, and it is false by consensus. And because of the saying that what you mentioned is not correct because it necessitates that equality. And because of the saying of Abraham, peace be upon him, 'but that my heart may be at ease' it indicates the acceptance of certain belief for increase as previously established. And it appears that the dominant assumption with which the possibility of the opposite does not occur to the mind has the same ruling as certainty in being true faith, for the faith of most of this category is like that. And on this, that faith-belief is susceptible to increase is completely clear. Second: from the two aspects of difference, namely that which is in relation to the object, it is said: detailed belief in the individuals of what is known that he brought is a part of faith, for which one is rewarded for his belief in it in detail, meaning that the individuals of what he brought are multiple and included in the general belief. So when he knows one of them specifically and believes in it, this is a belief different from that general belief and a part of faith. And there is no doubt that detailed [؟] beliefs accept increase, so too faith. And the texts such as His saying: 'And when His verses are recited to them, they increase them in faith' indicate its acceptance of both, i.e., faith's acceptance of increase and decrease by the second aspect, just as the text of His saying: 'but that my heart may be at ease' indicates its acceptance of both by the first aspect. His saying: 'And there is no doubt that detailed beliefs etc.' It is said: Since those details were already believed in their entirety summarily, so upon learning them, faith did not change from deficiency to increase but only from summary to detail. Yes, that difference is conceivable in the time of the Prophet, peace be upon him, because faith was belief in the entirety of what the Prophet brought, so whenever that entirety increased, the belief related to it increased necessarily. His saying: 'by the second aspect' he referred to its acceptance of both by the first aspect as well, considering this indication, namely the indication of His saying 'When His verses are recited...' is not unlikely, as is clear.
Source pages p. 361

Commentary
This passage is a discussion of how faith (iman) can increase. It begins by refuting an objection that the faith of the Prophet and ordinary believers would be equal, which is false by consensus. The answer points to two aspects. The first aspect is increase in the intensity of conviction, as shown by Prophet Ibrahim's request for reassurance. It also notes that a strong assumption that excludes the opposite in the mind has the same ruling as certainty. The second aspect is increase by detailed belief in specific items that were previously believed in summary. The commentator addresses a possible objection: learning details does not increase faith because the summary already included them; but the reply is that in the Prophet's time, the total body of revelation grew, so faith increased accordingly. The second footnote clarifies that the verse 'And when His verses are recited...' indicates increase by the second aspect as well.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Faith is a single monolithic thing that cannot increase or decrease; any change would mean it was incomplete.
Correction: Faith can increase in two ways: in the strength of certainty (intensity) and in the number of specific beliefs (detail). The Qur'an and consensus confirm this.

Key Takeaway
Faith increases in two ways: in its inner strength and in the number of specific beliefs held.

Definition of Kufr and the Ruling on Outward Actions
Defines kufr and answers objection about outward actions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that kufr is defined as the absence of tasdiq (affirmative belief) in the Messenger regarding necessary matters, and that outward actions contrary to Islam are treated as signs of denial, affecting external judgment but not necessarily internal belief.

Core Idea
Kufr is an inner absence of tasdiq, not merely an outward action.

In this passage, the author defines kufr as the opposite of faith: it is the lack of tasdiq concerning some of what is necessarily known to be from the Prophet. He then addresses a critical objection: if a person performs an outward act of disbelief like tying the zunnar but inwardly believes, are they a disbeliever? The answer distinguishes between external legal judgment and internal reality before God.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition of kufr
Read the opening lines carefully. The author defines kufr as 'lack of tasdiq of the Messenger in some of what is known necessarily that he brought.' Notice that kufr is defined by an inner state, not outward actions.
2
Identify the objection
The objection states that a person who ties the zunnar or wears distinctive non-Muslim clothing by choice, but internally believes, should not be considered a disbeliever. Understand why this seems problematic.
3
Understand the response
The author explains that such outward acts are made 'a sign of denial' (علامة للتكذيب). So the person is judged externally as a disbeliever, but if they had no intention of veneration, they are not a disbeliever before God. This shows the distinction between external ruling and internal reality.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المقصد الثالث : في الكفر ]
( في الكفر وهو خلاف الإيمان فهو عندنا عدم تصديق الرسول في بعض ما علم مجيئه ضرورة فإن قيل فشاد الزنار ولابس الغيار بالاختيار لا يكون كافراً) إذا كان مصدقاً له في الكل وهو باطل إجماعاً، (قلنا : جعلنا الشيء) الصادر عنه باختياره علامه للتكذيب فحكمنا عليه بذلك ، أي بكونه كافراً غير مصدق ولو علم أنه شد الزنار لا لتعظيم دين النصارى واعتقاد حقيته لم يحكم بكفره فيما بينه وبين الله، كما مر في سجود الشمس لا يقال : أطفال المؤمنين لا تصديق لهم، فيلزم أن يكونوا كفاراً لا مؤمنين وهو باطل لأنا نقول : هم مصدقون حكماً لما علم من ضرورة أنه الله كان يجعل إيمان أحد الأبوين إيماناً للأولاد.
قوله : ( لأنا) نقول : هم مصدقون حكماً إلخ) وبهذا أيضاً يندفع ما يتوهم من أنه يلزم أن لا يكون النائم مؤمناً، إذ لا تصديق له لأن النوم مضاد للعلم عندنا ووجه الاندفاع أن الشارع جعل التصديق المحقق في حكم الباقي ما لم يطرأ عليه ما يضاده فهو مصدق حكماً، وقد يجاب بأن التصديق ليس بإدراك بل هو كلام نفسي على ما وقع في كلام بعضهم ولا نسلم المنافاة بينه وبين النوم ولا يخفى ما فيه .
The third objective: on disbelief. (On disbelief, and it is the opposite of faith. It is for us: lack of tasdiq of the Messenger in some of what is known necessarily that he brought. For if it is said: the one who ties the zunnar and wears the distinctive garment by choice is not a disbeliever) if he is a believer in him in all, and it is false by consensus, (we say: we made the thing) that proceeds from him by his choice a sign of denial, so we judged him thereby, i.e., that he is a disbeliever without tasdiq, even if it is known that he tied the zunnar not for veneration of the religion of the Christians and belief in its truth, he is not judged to be a disbeliever between him and God, as passed in the prostration to the sun. It is not said: the children of believers have no tasdiq, so it would follow that they are disbelievers not believers, and it is false. For we say: they are believers by legal ruling, because it is known necessarily that God used to make the faith of one of the parents faith for the children. His saying: (for we say: they are believers by legal ruling etc.) And by this also is repelled what is imagined that it would follow that the sleeping person is not a believer, since he has no tasdiq, because sleep is opposed to knowledge according to us. And the way of repulsion is that the Lawgiver made the actual tasdiq in the ruling of remaining as long as nothing opposing it occurs, so he is a believer by ruling. And it may be answered that tasdiq is not perception but inner speech, as has occurred in the speech of some of them, and we do not concede the incompatibility between it and sleep, and what is in it is not hidden.
Source pages p. 361

Commentary
This passage defines kufr as the absence of tasdiq of the Messenger regarding something necessarily known to be from him. It then addresses an objection: if a person ties the zunnar (a belt) or wears distinctive non-Muslim clothing by choice, but internally believes in everything, are they a disbeliever? The answer is that such an act is made a sign of denial, so the person is judged a disbeliever externally, but if they did not intend veneration, they are not a disbeliever between themselves and God. Another objection concerns children of believers who have no actual tasdiq. The response is that they are considered believers by legal ruling because God imputes the faith of their parents to them. The footnote adds that this also answers the case of a sleeping person, who lacks tasdiq but is still considered a believer by ruling.

علامة التكذيب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that any outward action contrary to Islam makes one a disbeliever without exception.
Correction: The passage clarifies that outward actions are treated as signs of denial for external legal rulings, but the internal state (tasdiq) ultimately determines kufr or iman before God.

Key Takeaway

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you see someone perform an action that appears to go against Islam—like not praying or dressing immodestly—do you immediately assume they are a disbeliever? How does this lesson force you to pause and reconsider your judgment, knowing that only God knows the true state of their heart?
?
Think about a time you might have acted in a way that outwardly appeared un-Islamic due to fear or social pressure. Did you consider that before God, your intention might protect you from the label of disbelief? How does this lesson give you hope while also calling you to examine your own sincerity?
?
If your inner belief is hidden from all but Allah, what concrete steps can you take today to ensure your outward actions align with your inner tasdiq, not as a mere show, but as a genuine expression of faith?

Legal Imputation of Faith for Children and Sleepers
Addresses objections about children and sleepers not having tasdiq.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how children of believers and sleeping persons are considered believers despite lacking actual tasdiq, due to legal imputation and the permanence of tasdiq by legal ruling.

Core Idea
Tasdiq can be legally imputed to children and preserved for sleepers.

After defining kufr as lack of tasdiq, the author faces further objections: children of believers have no actual tasdiq, yet they are considered believers; similarly, a sleeping person has no tasdiq. The responses rely on legal rulings (ḥukm) and the concept of tasdiq as inner speech rather than perception.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection about children
The objection points out that children of believers have no tasdiq (affirmative belief) themselves, so according to the definition they should be considered disbelievers. Read how the author responds.
2
Understand the legal imputation
The author says children are 'believers by legal ruling' because it is known that God makes the faith of one of the parents count as faith for the children. This is a divine legal attribution.
This is not based on the child's own belief but on the parent's.
3
Consider the sleeping person
The author also addresses the case of a sleeping person. Since sleep is opposed to knowledge, a sleeper lacks actual tasdiq. Two answers are given: either the Lawgiver treats the previous tasdiq as remaining by legal ruling, or tasdiq is defined as inner speech, which is not incompatible with sleep.
The author notes that the second answer has issues.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المقصد الثالث : في الكفر ]
( في الكفر وهو خلاف الإيمان فهو عندنا عدم تصديق الرسول في بعض ما علم مجيئه ضرورة فإن قيل فشاد الزنار ولابس الغيار بالاختيار لا يكون كافراً) إذا كان مصدقاً له في الكل وهو باطل إجماعاً، (قلنا : جعلنا الشيء) الصادر عنه باختياره علامه للتكذيب فحكمنا عليه بذلك ، أي بكونه كافراً غير مصدق ولو علم أنه شد الزنار لا لتعظيم دين النصارى واعتقاد حقيته لم يحكم بكفره فيما بينه وبين الله، كما مر في سجود الشمس لا يقال : أطفال المؤمنين لا تصديق لهم، فيلزم أن يكونوا كفاراً لا مؤمنين وهو باطل لأنا نقول : هم مصدقون حكماً لما علم من ضرورة أنه الله كان يجعل إيمان أحد الأبوين إيماناً للأولاد.
قوله : ( لأنا) نقول : هم مصدقون حكماً إلخ) وبهذا أيضاً يندفع ما يتوهم من أنه يلزم أن لا يكون النائم مؤمناً، إذ لا تصديق له لأن النوم مضاد للعلم عندنا ووجه الاندفاع أن الشارع جعل التصديق المحقق في حكم الباقي ما لم يطرأ عليه ما يضاده فهو مصدق حكماً، وقد يجاب بأن التصديق ليس بإدراك بل هو كلام نفسي على ما وقع في كلام بعضهم ولا نسلم المنافاة بينه وبين النوم ولا يخفى ما فيه .
The third objective: on disbelief. (On disbelief, and it is the opposite of faith. It is for us: lack of tasdiq of the Messenger in some of what is known necessarily that he brought. For if it is said: the one who ties the zunnar and wears the distinctive garment by choice is not a disbeliever) if he is a believer in him in all, and it is false by consensus, (we say: we made the thing) that proceeds from him by his choice a sign of denial, so we judged him thereby, i.e., that he is a disbeliever without tasdiq, even if it is known that he tied the zunnar not for veneration of the religion of the Christians and belief in its truth, he is not judged to be a disbeliever between him and God, as passed in the prostration to the sun. It is not said: the children of believers have no tasdiq, so it would follow that they are disbelievers not believers, and it is false. For we say: they are believers by legal ruling, because it is known necessarily that God used to make the faith of one of the parents faith for the children. His saying: (for we say: they are believers by legal ruling etc.) And by this also is repelled what is imagined that it would follow that the sleeping person is not a believer, since he has no tasdiq, because sleep is opposed to knowledge according to us. And the way of repulsion is that the Lawgiver made the actual tasdiq in the ruling of remaining as long as nothing opposing it occurs, so he is a believer by ruling. And it may be answered that tasdiq is not perception but inner speech, as has occurred in the speech of some of them, and we do not concede the incompatibility between it and sleep, and what is in it is not hidden.
Source pages p. 361

Commentary
This passage defines kufr as the absence of tasdiq of the Messenger regarding something necessarily known to be from him. It then addresses an objection: if a person ties the zunnar (a belt) or wears distinctive non-Muslim clothing by choice, but internally believes in everything, are they a disbeliever? The answer is that such an act is made a sign of denial, so the person is judged a disbeliever externally, but if they did not intend veneration, they are not a disbeliever between themselves and God. Another objection concerns children of believers who have no actual tasdiq. The response is that they are considered believers by legal ruling because God imputes the faith of their parents to them. The footnote adds that this also answers the case of a sleeping person, who lacks tasdiq but is still considered a believer by ruling.

Key Takeaway
Children and sleepers are considered believers by legal ruling despite lacking actual tasdiq, either through imputation or preservation of previous tasdiq.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you sleep tonight, will you consciously entrust your faith to the legal ruling that it remains, or will you actively reaffirm your shahada before closing your eyes? What does your answer reveal about your reliance on God's mercy vs your own effort?
?
If your child is considered a believer by legal imputation from you, what does that obligate you to do in terms of teaching them actual faith? Are you content with the legal status alone, or do you feel a burden to ensure their heart truly affirms?
?
The passage offers two responses for the sleeper—one based on legal preservation and one on tasdiq as inner speech. Which one resonates more with your understanding of faith? Does your own inner speech of faith sustain you even when your mind is occupied? How can you strengthen that inner dialogue?

Kufr as Understood by Different Sects
Explains how various sects define kufr in opposition to their definitions of iman.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how each sect defines kufr as the opposite of its own definition of iman, and how the Mu'tazila classify sins into kufr and non-kufr categories.

Core Idea
Kufr is defined as the opposite of each sect's definition of iman.

Before we examine the specific definitions of kufr, we must first grasp a key principle: each sect defines kufr as the direct opposite of what it believes iman to be. This principle governs the ensuing discussion, as the author surveys three major views and then focuses on the Mu'tazila's detailed classification of sins.

Guided Path
1
Understand the general principle
Read the opening statement: kufr is the opposite of each sect's definition of iman. This sets the framework for the entire passage.
Notice that the author uses this principle to systematically present each view.
2
Examine the first view: iman as knowledge
According to this view, kufr is ignorance of God. The author quickly refutes it because it would imply Christians are believers.
This refutation is concise – note its logical basis.
3
Examine the second view: iman as obedience
This view is held by the Khawarij and some Mu'tazila. The Khawarij say every sin is kufr (refuted), while the Mu'tazila distinguish among three categories of sins.
Pay close attention to the Mu'tazila's three-fold division.
4
Understand the Mu'tazila classification of sins
The Mu'tazila divide sins into those indicating ignorance (kufr), those not indicating ignorance (two subcategories, one leading to the intermediate station).
The intermediate station is a distinctive Mu'tazili doctrine.
5
Consider the objection regarding the Salaf
A potential objection is raised: if the Salaf include actions in iman, would they also consider every sin as kufr? The answer distinguishes between the root meaning of iman (tasdiq) and the complete definition.
This shows the importance of precise definitions in theological debate.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهو أي الكفر عند كل طائفة مقابل ما فسره به الإيمان كما هو عندنا مقابل لما فسرناه به فمن قال : الإيمان معرفة الله قال الكفر هو الجهل بالله وبطلانه ظاهر ومن قال : الإيمان هو الطاعات كالخوارج وبعض المعتزلة قال : الكفر هو المعصية لكنهم اختلفوا فقالت الخوارج : كل معصية كفر، وقد أبطلناه وقالت المعتزلة المعاصي أقسام ثلاثة إذ منها ما يدل على الجهل بالله ووحدته وما يجوز عليه وما لا يجوز، والجهل برسالة رسوله كإلقاء المصحف في القاذورات واللفظ بكلمات دالة على ذلك وكسب الرسول والاستخفاف به فهو كفر ومنها ما لا يدل على ذلك وهو قسمان : قسم يخرج مرتكبه إلى منزلة بين المنزلتين أي الكفر والإيمان على معنى أنه لا يحكم على صاحبها بالكفر لسائر ما اتصف به من أعماله الصالحة، ولا
قوله : (وهو)
كل طائفة يقابل ما فسر به الإيمان رده في شرح المقاصد بأنه لا يستقيم على القول بالمنزلة بين المنزلتين أصلاً، ويمكن دفعه بأن التقابل لا يلزم أن يكون بالإيجاب والسلب حتى يرد ما ذكره فتأمل.
قوله : ( وبطلانه ظاهر لاستلزامه أن يكون النصارى مؤمنين .
قوله : ( فقالت :الخوارج كل معصية (كفر فإن قلت : يلزم السلف وأصحاب الأثر القائلين بأن الإيمان تصديق بالجنان وإقرار باللسان وعمل بالأركان أن يقولوا بما قال به الخوارج : بناء على أن الشيء ينتفي بانتفاء ركنه ، ولا منزلة عندهم بين الكفر والإيمان مع أنهم لا يجعلون تارك العمل خارجا من الإيمان ويقطعون بعدم خلوده في النار قلت : أجيب عنه بأن الإيمان يطلق على ما هو الأساس والأصل في دخول الجنة وهو التصديق وحده على ما هو الكامل المنجي، وهو الذي عد العمل ركناً منه وموضع الخلاف أن مطلق الاسم للأول أو الثاني، وقد أشرنا فيما سبق إلى وجه دفع آخر، فليتذكر.
And it, i.e., kufr, according to every sect is the opposite of what it interprets iman to be, just as it is with us the opposite of what we interpreted it to be. So whoever says: iman is knowledge of God, says kufr is ignorance of God, and its falsity is apparent. And whoever says: iman is acts of obedience, like the Khawarij and some of the Mu'tazila, says kufr is disobedience, but they differed. The Khawarij said: every act of disobedience is kufr, and we have refuted it. The Mu'tazila said: acts of disobedience are three divisions: some of them indicate ignorance of God and His oneness and what is permissible for Him and what is not, and ignorance of the message of His Messenger, like throwing the mushaf into filth and uttering words indicating that, and reviling the Messenger and showing contempt for him—that is kufr. And some of them do not indicate that, and they are two divisions: a division that takes its perpetrator to a station between the two stations, i.e., between kufr and iman, meaning that its possessor is not judged to be kufr because of the rest of his righteous deeds that he possesses, and not [the opposite?]. His saying: (And it) every sect opposes what it interprets iman to be, he refuted it in Sharh al-Maqasid by saying it is not sound at all on the view of the intermediate position. And it can be repelled by saying that opposition does not necessarily have to be by affirmation and negation so that what he mentioned would apply, so ponder. His saying: (and its falsity is apparent because it would require that the Christians be believers). His saying: (so the Khawarij said: every sin is kufr). For if you say: it would require that the Salaf and the people of athar who say that iman is affirmation with the heart, declaration with the tongue, and action with the limbs to say what the Khawarij said, based on the principle that a thing is negated by the negation of its pillar, and they do not have an intermediate station between kufr and iman, yet they do not consider the abandoner of action outside of iman and are certain that he will not be eternally in the Fire. I say: it was answered that iman is applied to what is the foundation and root for entering Paradise, which is tasdiq alone, as it is the perfect and salvific, and it is that which action was considered a pillar of it, and the point of disagreement is whether the absolute name belongs to the first or the second, and we have indicated another way of repulsion previously, so let it be remembered.
Source pages p. 362

Commentary
This passage defines kufr in relation to the definitions of iman held by various sects. It begins by stating that kufr is the opposite of each sect's definition of iman. It then reviews three views: 1) If iman is knowledge of God, then kufr is ignorance (refuted because it would make Christians believers). 2) The Khawarij say iman is acts of obedience, so kufr is disobedience; they consider every sin as kufr (refuted). 3) The Mu'tazila divide sins into three categories: those indicating ignorance (kufr), those that do not, and those leading to an intermediate station. The footnotes address objections: one argues that the Salaf, who include actions in the definition of iman, might also label every sin as kufr, but the answer distinguishes between the core meaning of iman (tasdiq) and the complete definition. The passage ends by urging remembrance of a previous repulsion.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All sects define kufr in the same way, usually as mere disbelief.
Correction: The passage shows that kufr is defined relative to each sect's definition of iman. For the Mu'tazila, not all sins are kufr; only those that indicate ignorance of God and His Messenger constitute kufr.

Checkpoint
According to the Mu'tazila, which of the following is considered kufr?
A) Any act of disobedience
B) Only sins indicating ignorance of God and His Messenger
C) Only major sins
D) Sins that do not indicate ignorance

Key Takeaway
Each sect defines kufr as the opposite of its own definition of iman, and the Mu'tazila further classify sins into those that constitute kufr and those that do not.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter a Muslim who commits a major sin, do you instinctively label them as having weak iman or even kufr? How does this lesson's distinction between the foundation of iman (tasdiq) and the complete definition (including actions) challenge your immediate reaction? Will you now stop and remember that only Allah judges the heart?
?
The Mu'tazila argued that certain sins reveal ignorance of God's attributes. Reflect on a sin you struggle with: does it stem from a moment where you forgot who Allah is? What would it take for you to internalize His greatness so deeply that the sin loses its appeal?
?
The Khawarij considered every sin as kufr, leading them to condemn fellow Muslims. Have you ever judged another believer harshly for a sin, forgetting that the line between iman and kufr is not yours to draw? How can you train your heart to hope for others' forgiveness as you hope for your own?

Classification of Disbelievers: Acknowledgment and Denial of Prophethood
Al-Jurjani classifies disbelievers and distinguishes denial by obstinacy or ijtihad.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three main categories of disbelievers and the distinction between denial out of obstinacy versus ijtihad.

Core Idea
Disbelievers are not a monolith; their cause of denial affects their punishment.

Al-Jurjani begins this appendix by systematically classifying mankind based on their stance toward the prophethood of Muhammad. He identifies several categories of those who do not acknowledge prophethood, and then distinguishes between denial rooted in obstinacy and denial based on ijtihad. This lays the groundwork for later discussions on salvation and punishment.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary division
Read the passage and notice the first split: those who acknowledge Muhammad's prophethood and those who do not.
This is the fundamental categorization.
2
Explore subdivisions of non-acknowledgers
Among those who do not acknowledge, there are those who acknowledge prophethood in general (Jews, Christians, Magians) and those who do not at all (further subdivided into Brahmins and Dahriyyun).
3
Understand the two causes of denial
Denial can be due to obstinacy (consensus: eternal punishment) or due to ijtihad without negligence (disputed, with al-Jahiz and al-Anbari excusing).
This distinction is crucial for kalam.
4
Reflect on the significance
Consider why this classification matters for discussions on faith, disbelief, and divine justice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تذنيب : في تفصيل الكفار فنقول : ( الإنسان إما معترف بنبوة محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم أو لا، والثاني : إما معترف بالنبوة في الجملة وهم اليهود والنصارى وغيرهم كالمجوس ( وإما غير معترف بها ( أصلا ( وهو إما معترف بالقادر المختار وهم البراهمة أو لا وهم الدهرية) على اختلاف أصنافهم ( ثم إنكارهم لنبوته إما عن عناد (وعذابه مخلداً إجماعاً) ، ( وإما عن اجتهاد به بلا تقصير، فالجاحظ والعنبري على أنه معذور وعذابه غير مخلد ، وقد عرفت أنه مخالف لإجماع من قبلهما، (و) الأول هو بكافر، ( المعترف بنبوته عليه الصلاة والسلام إما مخطئ في أصل من المسائل الأصولية ( وسنبين) في المقصد الخامس ) أنه ليس بكافر أو لا يكون مخطئاً في عقائده المتعلقة بأصول الدين ( وهو إما أن يكون اعتقاده ) عن برهان وهو ناج باتفاق، أو تقليد، وقد اختلف فيه فمن قال إنه (ناج بهذا الاعتقاد التقليدي ( فلأن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم حكم بإسلام من لم يعلم منه ذلك وهم الأكثرون، ومن قال : إنه غير ناج به فلان التصديق بالنبوة يتضمن العلم بدلالة المعجزة وإنه ) أي العلم بدلالة المعجزة على صدق النبي الله ) يتضمن العلم بما يجب اعتقاده ) في ذات تعالى وصفاته وأفعاله، فمن كان مصدقاً حقيقة كان عالماً بهذه الأمور كلها ( وإن لم يمكن له تنقيح الأدلة وتحريرها فإن ذلك ليس شرطاً في العلم والخروج عن التقليد، فمن لم يكن عالماً بها بأدلتها مفصلة ولا مجملة وكان مقلداً محضاً لم یکن مصدقاً حقيقة فلا يكون ناجياً، ولعل الأكثرين الذين حكم النبي بإسلامهم ونجاتهم كانوا من العالمين علماً إجمالياً كما مر في قصة الأعرابي لا من المقلدين تقليداً محضاً.
قوله : (وهم الدهرية المفهوم من شرح المقاصد أن الدهري أخص من ذلك لأنه قال : الكافر إن قال بقدم الدهر وإسناد الحوادث إليه خص باسم الدهري وإن كان لا يثبت الباري خص باسم المعطل.
Appendix: detailing the disbelievers. We say: (Man is either acknowledging the prophethood of Muhammad peace be upon him or not. The second is either acknowledging prophethood in general, and they are the Jews and Christians and others like the Magians, or not acknowledging it at all. And he is either acknowledging the Powerful and Free Chooser, and they are the Brahmins, or not, and they are the Dahriyyun (materialists) according to their different types. Then their denial of his prophethood is either out of obstinacy, and his punishment is eternal by consensus, or out of ijtihad without negligence, for al-Jahiz and al-'Anbari held that he is excused and his punishment is not eternal, and you have known that it is contrary to the consensus of those before them. And the first is a disbeliever. The one acknowledging his prophethood, peace be upon him, is either mistaken in one of the fundamental issues, and we will show in the fifth purpose that he is not a disbeliever, or not mistaken in his beliefs related to the principles of religion. And either his belief is from proof, and he is saved by consensus, or from imitation, and there is disagreement. Whoever said that he is saved by this imitative belief is because the Prophet peace be upon him judged the Islam of those from whom he did not know that, and they are the majority. And whoever said that he is not saved by it is because affirmation of prophethood entails knowledge of the indication of the miracle, and it i.e. knowledge of the indication of the miracle to the truthfulness of the Prophet of God entails knowledge of what must be believed of the Essence, attributes, and acts of the Exalted. So whoever is truly an affirmer is knowledgeable of all these matters, even if he cannot refine and articulate the proofs, for that is not a condition for knowledge and leaving imitation. So whoever is not knowledgeable of them with their detailed or summary proofs and is a pure imitator is not truly an affirmer and is not saved. Perhaps the majority whom the Prophet judged as Muslims and saved were from those possessing knowledge in summary form, as passed in the story of the Bedouin, not from the pure imitators. His statement: (and they are the Dahriyyun). The understanding from Sharh al-Maqasid is that the Dahri is more specific than that, because he said: the disbeliever, if he says by the pre-eternity of time and ascribing events to it, he is specifically called Dahri; but if he does not affirm the Creator, he is specifically called Mu'attil (denier of attributes).
Source pages p. 363

Commentary
This passage is a classification (tadhnīb) of disbelievers. The author divides mankind based on their stance toward the prophethood of Muhammad. First, those who acknowledge it (mu'tarif) and those who do not. Among those who do not acknowledge it, there are those who acknowledge prophethood in general (Jews, Christians, Magians) and those who do not acknowledge it at all. The latter are further divided into those who acknowledge a powerful free-chooser (al-Baramiha) and those who do not (al-Dahriyyun, materialists). Then the author considers the motive for denial: if out of obstinacy ('inad), punishment is eternal by consensus; if out of ijtihad without negligence, al-Jahiz and al-'Anbari excused them, but the author notes this contradicts earlier consensus. Those who acknowledge Muhammad's prophethood are divided: if they err in a fundamental issue (masa'il usuliyya), they are not disbelievers (as will be shown later); if they are correct in principles, their belief is either from proof (burhan) — saved by consensus — or from imitation (taqlid). The author explains the disagreement over imitative belief: those who deem it salvific point to the Prophet's acceptance of many seemingly imitative believers; those who deny it argue that true affirmation (tasdiq) entails knowledge of the miracle's indication, which implies knowledge of God's essence, attributes, and acts. A pure imitator without even summary knowledge is not truly an affirmer and is not saved. The author suggests that the majority judged as Muslims likely had summary knowledge (ilm ijmaili). A final note clarifies that 'Dahri' is a subset of those who deny the Creator, specifically those who posit the pre-eternity of time.

Key Terms
كفار
معترف بنبوة
يهود
نصارى
مجوس
براهمة
دهرية
عناد
اجتهاد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That all disbelievers are the same and their punishment is uniform.
Correction: The passage distinguishes between those who deny out of obstinacy (eternal punishment by consensus) and those who deny due to ijtihad without negligence (disputed, possibly excused).

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the consensus ruling on those who deny prophethood out of obstinacy?
A) They are excused and their punishment is not eternal.
B) Their punishment is eternal.
C) They are given a chance to repent.
D) They are considered Muslims.

Key Takeaway
The classification of disbelievers is not uniform; denial due to obstinacy leads to eternal punishment by consensus, while denial due to ijtihad is disputed.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter someone who denies a truth of Islam, do you immediately assume they are stubborn, or do you consider that they may be acting on sincere reasoning (ijtihad)? How would this shift your interaction with them?
?
The passage shows that even among those who reject prophethood, there are levels of acknowledgment and denial. Is your own heart more aligned with those who acknowledge prophethood in general but reject the specific, or are you fully submitted? What step can you take today to strengthen your acknowledgment of Muhammad's prophethood in a way that affects your daily choices?
?
If you knew that some disbelievers might be excused due to their ijtihad, would that change how you pray for their guidance? Are you willing to ask Allah to guide those who are sincerely mistaken, even if they oppose what you hold as truth?

The Status of Those Who Acknowledge Prophethood and the Debate on Imitative Belief
Al-Jurjani discusses the status of believers who err in fundamental issues and the debate on imitative belief.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rulings on those who acknowledge Muhammad's prophethood but err in fundamental issues, and the disagreement over whether imitative belief saves.

Core Idea
True affirmation of prophethood entails knowledge; pure imitation without summary knowledge does not save.

Having classified those who deny prophethood, al-Jurjani now turns to those who acknowledge it. He addresses two scenarios: error in fundamental issues and correctness in principles. This leads into a deep discussion on the nature of tasdiq (affirmation) and whether imitation (taqlid) suffices for salvation. The passage also clarifies the term 'Dahri'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the divisions among acknowledgers
Read the passage and note the two groups: those mistaken in fundamental issues (not kafir) and those correct in principles.
2
Understand the debate on proof vs imitation
Among the correct, belief can be from proof (saved by consensus) or imitation (disputed). Learn the arguments for and against imitative belief.
Proponents cite the Prophet's acceptance of many; opponents argue tasdiq requires knowledge of the miracle's implication.
3
Grasp the author's resolution
The author suggests that the majority had summary knowledge (ilm ijmail), not pure imitation, and only pure imitation fails to save.
Refer to the story of the Bedouin as an example.
4
Review the footnote on Dahri
The final note clarifies that 'Dahri' specifically refers to those who posit pre-eternal time, distinct from general deniers of the Creator (Mu'attil).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تذنيب : في تفصيل الكفار فنقول : ( الإنسان إما معترف بنبوة محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم أو لا، والثاني : إما معترف بالنبوة في الجملة وهم اليهود والنصارى وغيرهم كالمجوس ( وإما غير معترف بها ( أصلا ( وهو إما معترف بالقادر المختار وهم البراهمة أو لا وهم الدهرية) على اختلاف أصنافهم ( ثم إنكارهم لنبوته إما عن عناد (وعذابه مخلداً إجماعاً) ، ( وإما عن اجتهاد به بلا تقصير، فالجاحظ والعنبري على أنه معذور وعذابه غير مخلد ، وقد عرفت أنه مخالف لإجماع من قبلهما، (و) الأول هو بكافر، ( المعترف بنبوته عليه الصلاة والسلام إما مخطئ في أصل من المسائل الأصولية ( وسنبين) في المقصد الخامس ) أنه ليس بكافر أو لا يكون مخطئاً في عقائده المتعلقة بأصول الدين ( وهو إما أن يكون اعتقاده ) عن برهان وهو ناج باتفاق، أو تقليد، وقد اختلف فيه فمن قال إنه (ناج بهذا الاعتقاد التقليدي ( فلأن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم حكم بإسلام من لم يعلم منه ذلك وهم الأكثرون، ومن قال : إنه غير ناج به فلان التصديق بالنبوة يتضمن العلم بدلالة المعجزة وإنه ) أي العلم بدلالة المعجزة على صدق النبي الله ) يتضمن العلم بما يجب اعتقاده ) في ذات تعالى وصفاته وأفعاله، فمن كان مصدقاً حقيقة كان عالماً بهذه الأمور كلها ( وإن لم يمكن له تنقيح الأدلة وتحريرها فإن ذلك ليس شرطاً في العلم والخروج عن التقليد، فمن لم يكن عالماً بها بأدلتها مفصلة ولا مجملة وكان مقلداً محضاً لم یکن مصدقاً حقيقة فلا يكون ناجياً، ولعل الأكثرين الذين حكم النبي بإسلامهم ونجاتهم كانوا من العالمين علماً إجمالياً كما مر في قصة الأعرابي لا من المقلدين تقليداً محضاً.

Appendix: detailing the disbelievers. We say: (Man is either acknowledging the prophethood of Muhammad peace be upon him or not. The second is either acknowledging prophethood in general, and they are the Jews and Christians and others like the Magians, or not acknowledging it at all. And he is either acknowledging the Powerful and Free Chooser, and they are the Brahmins, or not, and they are the Dahriyyun (materialists) according to their different types. Then their denial of his prophethood is either out of obstinacy, and his punishment is eternal by consensus, or out of ijtihad without negligence, for al-Jahiz and al-'Anbari held that he is excused and his punishment is not eternal, and you have known that it is contrary to the consensus of those before them. And the first is a disbeliever. The one acknowledging his prophethood, peace be upon him, is either mistaken in one of the fundamental issues, and we will show in the fifth purpose that he is not a disbeliever, or not mistaken in his beliefs related to the principles of religion. And either his belief is from proof, and he is saved by consensus, or from imitation, and there is disagreement. Whoever said that he is saved by this imitative belief is because the Prophet peace be upon him judged the Islam of those from whom he did not know that, and they are the majority. And whoever said that he is not saved by it is because affirmation of prophethood entails knowledge of the indication of the miracle, and it i.e. knowledge of the indication of the miracle to the truthfulness of the Prophet of God entails knowledge of what must be believed of the Essence, attributes, and acts of the Exalted. So whoever is truly an affirmer is knowledgeable of all these matters, even if he cannot refine and articulate the proofs, for that is not a condition for knowledge and leaving imitation. So whoever is not knowledgeable of them with their detailed or summary proofs and is a pure imitator is not truly an affirmer and is not saved. Perhaps the majority whom the Prophet judged as Muslims and saved were from those possessing knowledge in summary form, as passed in the story of the Bedouin, not from the pure imitators. His statement: (and they are the Dahriyyun). The understanding from Sharh al-Maqasid is that the Dahri is more specific than that, because he said: the disbeliever, if he says by the pre-eternity of time and ascribing events to it, he is specifically called Dahri; but if he does not affirm the Creator, he is specifically called Mu'attil (denier of attributes).
Source pages p. 363

Commentary
This passage is a classification (tadhnīb) of disbelievers. The author divides mankind based on their stance toward the prophethood of Muhammad. First, those who acknowledge it (mu'tarif) and those who do not. Among those who do not acknowledge it, there are those who acknowledge prophethood in general (Jews, Christians, Magians) and those who do not acknowledge it at all. The latter are further divided into those who acknowledge a powerful free-chooser (al-Baramiha) and those who do not (al-Dahriyyun, materialists). Then the author considers the motive for denial: if out of obstinacy ('inad), punishment is eternal by consensus; if out of ijtihad without negligence, al-Jahiz and al-'Anbari excused them, but the author notes this contradicts earlier consensus. Those who acknowledge Muhammad's prophethood are divided: if they err in a fundamental issue (masa'il usuliyya), they are not disbelievers (as will be shown later); if they are correct in principles, their belief is either from proof (burhan) — saved by consensus — or from imitation (taqlid). The author explains the disagreement over imitative belief: those who deem it salvific point to the Prophet's acceptance of many seemingly imitative believers; those who deny it argue that true affirmation (tasdiq) entails knowledge of the miracle's indication, which implies knowledge of God's essence, attributes, and acts. A pure imitator without even summary knowledge is not truly an affirmer and is not saved. The author suggests that the majority judged as Muslims likely had summary knowledge (ilm ijmaili). A final note clarifies that 'Dahri' is a subset of those who deny the Creator, specifically those who posit the pre-eternity of time.

معترف بنبوة
مسائل أصولية
برهان
تقليد
علم إجمالي
دهري

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That imitative belief is automatically salvific without any knowledge.
Correction: The passage shows disagreement and requires at least summary knowledge of the proof for true affirmation.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the condition for true affirmation (tasdiq) of prophethood?
A) Detailed knowledge of all proofs.
B) Knowledge of the implication of the miracle.
C) Following the majority.
D) None of the above.

Key Takeaway
True affirmation of prophethood requires at least summary knowledge of the proof; pure imitation without knowledge is not salvific.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever examined the evidence for your belief in Allah and His prophets, or do you realize you are simply following what you were raised with? If your faith is only imitation, what will you do to acquire the summary knowledge that the passage says is necessary?
?
The passage distinguishes between a true affirmer who has knowledge and a pure imitator. Which category describes you right now, and why haven't you sought certainty if you are in the second?
?
Imagine standing before Allah and being asked: 'Did you know the proof of My existence and guidance, or did you just assume?' If your answer is imitation, are you willing to risk your salvation on that? What step will you take today to move from imitation to true affirmation?

Views on the Major Sinner and the First Kharijite Proof
Presents the three views on major sin and responds to the first Kharijite proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three main views on the status of a Muslim who commits a major sin and the first argument of the Khawarij from verse 5:44, along with the response that the verse does not refer to sinful believers.

Core Idea
A major sin does not remove one from faith; the verse about judging is not about the sinful believer.

This passage addresses a critical question in Islamic theology: what happens to a Muslim who commits a major sin? Three early sects gave different answers. The Khawarij argued from a Qur'anic verse that such a person is a disbeliever. Let's examine their proof and the response that clarifies the verse's true meaning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three positions
Read the opening to find the views of the Khawarij, Hasan al-Basri, and the Mu'tazila.
2
Examine the Kharijite argument
Look at how they use verse 5:44 to argue that the sinful believer is a disbeliever.
They rely on the word 'whoever' as general.
3
Understand the response
See the two responses: first, that the verse refers to someone who never judges by any revelation; second, that it refers to the Jews.
The response shows that the verse is not about the sinful Muslim.

) في أن مرتكب الكبيرة من أهل الصلاة أي من أهل القبلة ( مؤمن، وقد تقدم في مسألة حقيقة الإيمان، وغرضنا هاهنا ذكر مذهب المخالفين. والجواب عن شبهتهم : ذهب الخوارج إلى أنه كافر والحسن البصري إلى أنه منافق، والمعتزلة إلى أنه لا مؤمن ولا كافر حجة الخارج وجوه : الأول : قوله تعالى : ومن لم يحكم بما أنزل الله فأولئك هم الكافرون ﴾ [المائدة : ٤٤] ، فإن كلمة من عامة في كل من لم يحكم بما أنزل فيدخل فيه الفاسق المصدق، وأيضاً فقد علل كفرهم بعدم الحكم فكل من لم يحكم بما أنزل الله كان كافراً، والفاسق لم يحكم بما أنزل الله (قلنا : ) الموصولات لم توضع للعموم بل هي للجنس تحتمل العموم والخصوص، فنقول : المراد من لم يحكم بشيء مما أنزل الله أصلاً) ولا نزاع في كونه كافراً ، ( أو ) نقول : المراد بما أنزل الله ) هو التوراة بقرينة ما قبله وهو إنا أنزلنا التوراة ﴾ [المائدة : ٤٤] الآية، وأمتنا غير متعبدين بالحكم فيختص باليهود فيلزم أن يكونوا كافرين إذا لم يحكموا بالتوراة، ونحن نقول بموجبه. ( الثاني : ( من تلك الوجوه : قوله تعالى : وهل يجازي إلا الكفور ﴾ [سبأ : ۱۷] ) فإنه يدل على أنه كل من يجازى فهو كافر، وصاحب الكبيرة ممن يجازى لقوله: ﴿ ومن يقتل مؤمناً متعمداً فجزاؤه جهنم
قوله : (ذهب الخوارج إلى أنه (كافر وذهب الأزارقة إلى أنه مشترك لأنه يعمل عملاً لله تعالى، وعملاً لغيره وهو نفسه أو الشيطان أو غيرهما. قوله : ( والحسن البصري إلى أنه (منافق أي مظهر للإيمان مبطن للكفر، وأصله من نافق اليربوع أي أخذ في نافقائه وهي إحدى جحريه يكتمها ويظهر غيرها، وهو موضع يرفعه، فإذا أتى من قبل القاصعاء وهو جحره الذي يقصع فيه أي يدخل ضرب النافقاء برأسه فينفق ويخرج منه، والحق أن مذهب الحسن راجع إلى مذهب الخوارج ولا يمكن حمل كلامه على أنه مؤمن في الجملة وإن لم يكن مؤمناً كاملاً، لأن الوجه الثاني من وجهي استدلاله على مذهبه يدل على عدم الاعتقاد فيكون كافراً، اللهم إلا أن يراد بنفي الاعتقاد تضعيفه على نمط قولهم : زيد ليس بشيء وعلى هذا يؤول إلى كلام أهل السنة والمشهور خلافه وفي بعض الكتب أن الحسن البصري رجع عن هذا المذهب.
قوله : (المراد من لم يحكم بشيء مما أنزل الله تعالى أصلاً) وقد يجاب بأن الحكم بالشيء التصديق به، ولا شك أن من لم يصدق بما أنزل الله تعالى فهو كافر، وليس بشيء لأن السياق صريح في أن المراد بالحكم بما أنزل الله تعالى هو القضاء فيما بين الناس بما يوافقه لا معناه الاصطلاحي الذي هو التصديق.
The fourth objective: On the fact that the committer of a major sin from the people of prayer, i.e., from the people of the qibla, is a believer. It has preceded in the issue of the reality of faith, and our purpose here is to mention the doctrine of the opponents and the response to their doubts. The Khawarij went to the view that he is a disbeliever, and Hasan al-Basri to the view that he is a hypocrite, and the Mu'tazila to the view that he is neither a believer nor a disbeliever. The proof of the Kharijite has aspects: The first: His statement, the Most High: 'And whoever does not judge by what Allah has revealed – then it is those who are the disbelievers' [5:44], for the word 'whoever' is general in every one who does not judge by what was revealed, so it includes the sinful verifier. Also, He has caused their disbelief to be conditioned upon not judging, so everyone who does not judge by what Allah has revealed is a disbeliever, and the sinful person does not judge by what Allah has revealed. We say: The relative pronouns were not placed for generality, but rather for the genus, bearing generality and specificity. So we say: The intended meaning is one who does not judge by anything of what Allah has revealed at all, and there is no dispute that he is a disbeliever. Or we say: The intended meaning by 'what Allah has revealed' is the Torah, by the context of what precedes it, which is 'Indeed, We sent down the Torah' [5:44] the verse, and our nation is not obligated to judge by it, so it is specific to the Jews, so it follows that they are disbelievers if they do not judge by the Torah, and we affirm its implication. The second of those aspects: His statement, the Most High: 'And do We recompense except the ungrateful?' [34:17], for it indicates that everyone who is recompensed is a disbeliever, and the committer of a major sin is among those who are recompensed because of His statement: 'And whoever kills a believer intentionally, his recompense is Hell' [...] Commentator's note: The Khawarij went to the view that he is a disbeliever, and the Azariqa went to the view that he is a polytheist because he does a deed for Allah and a deed for other than Him, whether himself, Satan, or others. Note: Hasan al-Basri went to the view that he is a hypocrite, i.e., one who outwardly shows faith and inwardly conceals disbelief. Its origin is from the jerboa's 'nifaq' – it takes to its 'nafiqa' which is one of its two burrows, hiding it and showing the other. It is a place which it raises, so when it comes from the direction of the 'qasi'a' which is its burrow where it enters, it strikes the 'nafiqa' with its head and emerges from it. And the truth is that the doctrine of Hasan returns to the doctrine of the Khawarij, and his statement cannot be interpreted as meaning he is a believer in general, even if not a perfect believer, because the second of the two aspects of his reasoning for his doctrine indicates lack of belief, so he is a disbeliever, unless by 'negation of belief' is meant its weakness, in the manner of their saying: 'Zaid is nothing.' On this basis it returns to the statement of Ahl al-Sunna, but the famous view is otherwise, and in some books it is said that Hasan al-Basri recanted this doctrine. Commentator's note: The intended meaning is 'one who does not judge by anything of what Allah has revealed at all.' And it may be answered that 'judging by something' is affirming it, and there is no doubt that whoever does not affirm what Allah has revealed is a disbeliever, but it is nothing because the context is explicit that the intended meaning of 'judging by what Allah has revealed' is the judgment among people in accordance with it, not its technical meaning which is affirmation.
Source pages p. 364

Commentary
This passage addresses the status of a Muslim who commits a major sin. It first states the mainstream view that he remains a believer, then presents the views of the Khawarij (disbeliever), Hasan al-Basri (hypocrite), and the Mu'tazila (neither believer nor disbeliever). The passage then presents the first proof of the Khawarij: the Qur'anic verse 'Whoever does not judge by what Allah has revealed – those are the disbelievers' (5:44). The Kharijite argues that the word 'whoever' is general and includes the sinful believer, and that the verse makes disbelief conditional on not judging, so the sinful person qualifies. The response is that relative pronouns like 'man' are not put for generality but for the genus, allowing specification. Two answers are given: first, the verse refers only to one who never judges by anything of Allah's revelation at all; second, the context shows it refers specifically to the Jews, as the verse is about the Torah. The passage then mentions a second argument from 34:17, but does not give a response; instead, it goes into explanatory notes. The notes clarify the Kharijite view and the view of the Azariqa that the sinner is a polytheist. It also explains Hasan al-Basri's view that he is a hypocrite, tracing the etymology of 'nifaq' to the jerboa's burrows. The commentary argues that Hasan's view essentially returns to the Kharijite position, since his reasoning indicates lack of belief, unless 'negation of belief' is interpreted as weakness, which would align with Ahl al-Sunna. Finally, there is a note on the first response to the verse, explaining that 'judging' in the verse refers to judicial ruling, not mental affirmation, so the sinful believer who does not rule by the revelation but still affirms it is not included.

الخوارج
الحسن البصري
المعتزلة
الآية ٥:٤٤
الموصولات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Verse 5:44 declares every Muslim who commits a major sin to be a disbeliever.
Correction: The verse is about those who totally reject Allah's law, not about a believer who sins. The response explains that the verse either refers to someone who never judges by any revelation or is contextually about the Jews.

Checkpoint
According to the response to the Kharijite argument from verse 5:44, what is the intended meaning of 'whoever does not judge by what Allah has revealed'?
A) Every Muslim who commits a major sin
B) Whoever does not judge by anything of Allah's revelation at all
C) Whoever judges according to his own desires
D) The Jews who did not judge by the Torah

Key Takeaway
A Muslim who commits a major sin is still a believer; the verse 5:44 does not apply to him because it refers to total rejection or to the Jews.

?

Sixth Khariji Proof: Light Scales and the Response
Al-Jurjani refutes sixth Khariji proof using Qur'an 23:105 and discusses a problem with the response.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the sixth Khariji proof based on light scales, the Ahl al-Sunna response that faith outweighs sins, and the subtle problem al-Jurjani raises about the punishment of sins.

Core Idea
Faith makes the scales heavy, but does that cancel punishment for sins?

The sixth Khariji argument seizes on the verse about light scales to argue that major sinners are deniers and thus unbelievers. The Ahl al-Sunna respond that faith makes the scales heavy, removing the sinner from the verse's scope. However, this response raises a further question about the punishment of sins.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic source and translation once. Notice the structure: proof, response, and a critical discussion.
The passage is dense; take your time.
2
Identify the Khariji logic
Work through the Kharijite syllogism: major sinner has few good deeds → scales light → included in verse → denier → unbeliever.
Pay attention to how they connect 'light scales' to 'denial'.
3
Understand the Ahl al-Sunna response
The response asserts that faith (iman) makes the scales heavy, so the believer does not fall under the verse. Ask: why does faith outweigh sins?
This is a key doctrinal point.
4
Examine the problem al-Jurjani notes
If scales are heavy because of faith, does that mean sins go unpunished? The Qur'an says those with heavy scales are in a pleasant life. How is this reconciled?
Al-Jurjani does not resolve it, only flags the discussion.
5
Reflect on the implication
Consider how this debate illustrates the tension between divine justice and mercy. What is the standard Ahl al-Sunna position?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السادس : قوله تعالى : في حق من خفت موازينه ألم تكن آياتي تتلى عليكم فكنتم بها تكذبونه [المؤمنون : ١٠٥] ، و ( حينئذ نقول : (الفاسق ممن خفت موازينه ) لقلة حسناته، وكل من خفت موازينه فهو مكذب بالآية المذكورة وكل مكذب كافر، قلنا : بل ثقلت) موازين الفاسق (بالإيمان فلا يندرج فيمن خفت موازينه .
قوله : (ثقلت بالإيمان) فيه بحث لأنه يؤدي إلى نفي جزاء المعصية مع الإيمان لأن من ثقلت موازينه فهو في عيشة راضية على ما نطق به القرآن وحمله على أن عاقبته ذلك لم يقل به
The sixth: His statement, exalted is He, concerning those whose scales are light: 'Were not My verses recited to you, and you used to deny them?' (al-Mu'minun 23:105). And then we say: The sinful person is among those whose scales are light because of the fewness of his good deeds, and everyone whose scales are light is a denier of the mentioned verse, and every denier is an unbeliever. We say: Rather, the scales of the sinful person are heavy because of faith, so he does not fall among those whose scales are light. His statement: 'Heavy because of faith' – there is a discussion about this because it leads to negating the punishment of disobedience along with faith, since the one whose scales are heavy is in a pleasant life, as the Qur'an states, and interpreting it as meaning that his end will be that, no one says that.
Source pages p. 365

Commentary
The sixth Khariji proof uses Qur'an 23:105, where Allah rebukes those with light scales, saying 'Were not My verses recited to you, so you used to deny them?' The Kharijites argue that the major sinner has few good deeds, so his scales are light, making him a denier and thus an unbeliever. The response asserts that the believer's scales are heavy due to faith (iman), even if his deeds are few. Faith outweighs all sins, so his scales are not light. Therefore he is not included in the verse's rebuke. The commentator notes a problem with this response: if scales are heavy only because of faith, then sin would be unpunished, but the Qur'an says those with heavy scales are in a pleasant life, implying no punishment. This seems to negate the punishment for sin along with faith. However, the commentator simply mentions that there is a debate; the response as given is the standard Ahl al-Sunna position that faith outweighs sins, but the issue of punishment remains. The commentator does not resolve it here.

Key Terms
الموازين
خفت
ثقلت
الإيمان
التكذيب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Kharijites assume that scales of deeds determine one's status in the afterlife solely by good deeds, ignoring the decisive weight of faith.
Correction: The Ahl al-Sunna affirm that faith (iman) is the heaviest weight on the scales, so even a sinful believer's scales are heavy, thus not subject to the verse's condemnation. However, this does not mean sins go unpunished—punishment may still occur before entering paradise.

Checkpoint
How does the Ahl al-Sunna respond to the sixth Khariji proof about light scales?
A) By saying the major sinner's scales are light
B) By saying the major sinner's scales are heavy because of his faith
C) By denying that the verse applies to anyone
D) By saying the major sinner will not be punished

Key Takeaway
Faith outweighs sins, so a believer's scales are heavy, but the relationship between faith and punishment remains a subtle theological question.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you secretly rely on your faith to excuse sins you commit, assuming your scales are heavy enough? What specific sin have you not repented from because you think your iman outweighs it?
?
If faith alone prevented punishment, would you still fear Allah's justice? How does this lesson challenge your balance between hope in mercy and fear of accountability?
?
When you read that the deniers are rebuked in the Qur'an, do you see yourself in that warning? In what ways do you deny Allah's verses through your actions rather than your words?

The Sinner as Wrongdoer and the Proof from Quran
Sanusi presents the thirteenth proof and refutes it by reductio ad absurdum using prophets.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the thirteenth proof attempts to equate wrongdoing with disbelief and why the prophets' confessions of wrongdoing refute that argument.

Core Idea
A verse that curses wrongdoers cannot make all wrongdoers disbelievers.

Sanusi presents a proof that every sinner is a wrongdoer and every wrongdoer is a disbeliever, citing Quran 11:18-19. But this argument leads to an absurdity: prophets admitted wrongdoing. This lesson shows how the verse is limited by a specifying attribute.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the structure: a statement of the proof, a Quranic citation, a refutation using prophets, and a solution.
Pay attention to the names of the prophets and their statements.
2
Identify the proof and its basis
The proof claims that every wrongdoer is a disbeliever. The basis is Quran 11:18-19, which curses wrongdoers and calls them disbelievers.
But the verse describes wrongdoers who also turn people from Allah's way.
3
Understand the refutation using prophets
The response argues that if every wrongdoer were a disbeliever, then the prophets who admitted wrongdoing would be disbelievers. This is impossible.
Adam, Moses, and Jonah all confessed wrongdoing.
4
Learn the solution: the specifying attribute
The solution is that the verse describes wrongdoers with a specific attribute—those who avert others from Allah's way—so it does not apply to all wrongdoers like the prophets.
This preserves the prophets' status while limiting the verse.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثالث عشر: ( الفاسق ظالم على غيره أو على نفسه وكل ظالم كافر لقوله تعالى: ( ألا لعنة الله على الظالمين الذين يصدون عن سبيل الله ويبغونها عوجاً بالآخرة هم كافرون ﴾ [ هود : ۱۸ - ۱۹]، قلنا يلزم مما ذكرتم تكفير الأنبياء حيث اعترفوا بظلمهم، فإنه قال آدم وحواء: ربنا ظلمنا أنفسنا، وقال موسى: إني ظلمت نفسي، وقال يونس: إني كنت من الظالمين وحله أن يقال ما ذكر بعد الظالمين صفة مخصصة فلا يلزم تكفير كل ظاهر. قوله: أنك من تدخل النار فقد أخزيته لا يقال: هذا حكاية كلام الأبرار ولا يمتنع الكذب عليهم لأنا نقول: هو في معرض التصديق عرفاً، نعم يمكن أن يقال: يحتمل أن يكون أخزيته من الخزاية لا من الخزي فلا يتكرر الوسط في القياس الذي ذكره ولا يتم الاستدلال على أن الخزي الذي يكون اليوم ظرفاً له خزي خاص فلعله خزي يوم الحساب لا خزي يوم دخول النار.
The thirteenth: The sinner is a wrongdoer against others or against himself, and every wrongdoer is a disbeliever, due to His saying, exalted be He: 'Indeed, the curse of Allah is upon the wrongdoers who avert [people] from the way of Allah and seek to make it crooked, and they, concerning the Hereafter, are disbelievers' [Hud 11:18-19]. We said: From what you have mentioned, the condemnation of the prophets as disbelievers follows, since they confessed their wrongdoing. For Adam and Eve said: 'Our Lord, we have wronged ourselves,' and Moses said: 'Indeed, I have wronged myself,' and Jonah said: 'Indeed, I was among the wrongdoers.' Its solution is that what is mentioned after 'the wrongdoers' is a specifying attribute (ṣifa mukhaṣṣiṣa), so it is not necessary to condemn every apparent wrongdoer. [Objection:] His saying: 'Indeed, whoever You admit to the Fire, You have disgraced him' – it cannot be said that this is a narration of the speech of the righteous and that lying is not impossible for them, for we say: It is in the context of affirmation customarily. Yes, it can be said: It is possible that 'disgraced him' (akhzaytahu) is from khazāya (shame) not from khizy (disgrace), so the middle term in the syllogism mentioned does not recur, and the inference is not completed that the disgrace which is today a circumstance for it is a specific disgrace, perhaps it is disgrace on the Day of Reckoning, not disgrace on the day of entering the Fire.
Source pages p. 367

Commentary
This passage presents the thirteenth proof, arguing that the sinner is a wrongdoer (ẓālim) and Quran 11:18-19 curses wrongdoers and calls them disbelievers. The response refutes this by reductio ad absurdum: if every wrongdoer were a disbeliever, the prophets who admitted wrongdoing (Adam, Moses, Jonah) would be disbelievers, which is impossible. The solution is that the verse describes wrongdoers who also 'avert from the way of Allah' etc., so the description is specifying (ṣifa mukhaṣṣiṣa), not applying to all wrongdoers. Then there is an additional objection-answer concerning the verse 'whoever You admit to the Fire, You have disgraced him' (from the eleventh proof). The objector says this might be a report of the speech of the righteous, but lying is not impossible for them (i.e., the prophets? unclear). The answer says it is in a context of affirmation (taṣdīq) customarily. Then the responder suggests an alternative interpretation: 'akhzaytahu' might be derived from khazāya (shame) rather than khizy (disgrace), so the syllogism does not hold; perhaps the disgrace is only on the Day of Reckoning, not on entering the Fire.

Key Terms
ظالم
الأنبياء
صفة مخصصة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Every wrongdoer is a disbeliever because the Quran curses 'the wrongdoers' in general.
Correction: The Quran specifically curses those wrongdoers who also 'avert from the way of Allah and seek to make it crooked,' so it does not condemn all wrongdoers.

Checkpoint
Why does the response argue that the verse from Hud (11:18-19) cannot condemn all wrongdoers as disbelievers?
A) Because the verse is abrogated by later revelations.
B) Because the prophets admitted wrongdoing, so they would be disbelievers, which is impossible.
C) Because the verse refers only to polytheists, not monotheists.
D) Because the sinner repents before death.

Key Takeaway
The verse from Hud does not condemn all wrongdoers but only those who also avert people from Allah's way, so the proof that every wrongdoer is a disbeliever fails.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read a verse like 'the curse of Allah is upon the wrongdoers,' do you ever assume it applies to people you consider 'wrongdoers' in your own judgment, without considering the full context? How might you be misusing the Quran like the opponents in this lesson?
?
The prophets confessed their wrongdoing openly—Adam, Moses, Jonah. Are you willing to admit your faults before Allah with the same humility, or do you hide behind excuses? What would change in your prayers if you truly said 'rabbanā ẓalamnā anfusanā'?
?
This lesson shows how a specific attribute in a verse can completely change its application. Are there verses you have been applying too broadly in your own life—perhaps condemning yourself or others unfairly? What would it take for you to go back and study the specifying attributes?

The Objection about Disgrace in the Fire
Sanusi presents an objection-answer concerning the derived meaning of 'disgrace' from the word 'akhzaytahu'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the subtle objection regarding the word 'akhzaytahu' and how it can be interpreted to avoid the conclusion of universal disgrace.

Core Idea
A single word's root can change the entire argument.

After the main refutation, Sanusi addresses an additional objection concerning the verse 'Whoever You admit to the Fire, You have disgraced him.' The discussion reveals a linguistic nuance that may dismantle the proof's syllogism.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection passage
Read the Arabic and translation of this section. The objection involves a verse from the eleventh proof about disgrace in the Fire.
The objector questions whether the verse can be taken as a general proof.
2
Understand the first response
The first response argues that the verse is in a context of affirmation (taṣdīq), so it is not a mere report of speech that could be false.
This counters the objection that it might be a report of righteous people who could lie.
3
Analyze the alternative derivation
The alternative solution proposes that 'akhzaytahu' might derive from khazāya (shame) rather than khizy (disgrace). This breaks the syllogism because the middle term does not recur.
Also, the disgrace might be specific to the Day of Reckoning, not to entering the Fire.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

The thirteenth: The sinner is a wrongdoer against others or against himself, and every wrongdoer is a disbeliever, due to His saying, exalted be He: 'Indeed, the curse of Allah is upon the wrongdoers who avert [people] from the way of Allah and seek to make it crooked, and they, concerning the Hereafter, are disbelievers' [Hud 11:18-19]. Commentary
This passage presents the thirteenth proof, arguing that the sinner is a wrongdoer (ẓālim) and Quran 11:18-19 curses wrongdoers and calls them disbelievers. The response refutes this by reductio ad absurdum: if every wrongdoer were a disbeliever, the prophets who admitted wrongdoing (Adam, Moses, Jonah) would be disbelievers, which is impossible. Correction: It can also derive from khazāya meaning 'shame', and the context may refer to a specific shame on the Day of Reckoning, not general disgrace.

The Fourteenth Proof: Sinners in the Quran
Sanusi refutes the 14th proof by showing it implies universal denial of Resurrection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Sanusi refutes the claim that Quran 32:20 proves every sinner is a disbeliever by showing its apparent meaning leads to an absurdity.

Core Idea
Quranic threats cannot be taken literally if they lead to false consequences.

The fourteenth objection argues that a verse threatening sinners with eternal fire implies all sinners are disbelievers. But Sanusi points out that the verse's apparent meaning would require every sinner to deny the Resurrection, which is obviously false. This lesson unpacks that refutation.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and response
Read the Arabic and translation of the fourteenth proof and its answer. Notice how the objector uses the verse to claim that 'sinner' means 'disbeliever'.
The verse is about those who 'defiantly disobey' (fasaqū).
2
Identify the absurd consequence
Sanusi argues that taking the verse literally would mean every sinner denies the Resurrection. Ask yourself: is that true? Why is it a problem?
This is a classic reductio ad absurdum argument.
3
Understand the principle
The response shows that a text's apparent generality can be abandoned if it leads to a certain falsehood. This is a key hermeneutical principle in kalam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الرابع عشر : قوله تعالى : وأما الذين فسقوا فمأواهم النار ﴾ [السجدة : ٢٠] الآية ) وتمامها كلما أرادوا أن يخرجوا منها أعيدوا فيها وقيل لهم ذوقوا عذاب النار الذي كنتم به تكذبون ﴾ [السجدة : ٢٠ ]، فإنه يدل على أن كل فاسق كافر ( قلنا : ) ليس قوله : وأما الذين فسقوا ﴾ [السجدة : ٢٠ ]، باقياً على عمومه الظاهر لأنه ( يقتضي أن كل فاسق مكذب بالقيامة وإنه باطل قطعاً. الخامس عشر قوله تعالى: يتساءلون عن المجرمين ما سلككم في سقر [المدثر : ٤٠-٤٢ ] إلى قوله : وكنا نكذب بيوم الدين ﴾ [المدثر : ٤٦] فثبت بذلك أن كل مجرم داخل في النار كافر ولا شبهة في أن الفاسق مجرم لا يدخل النار، قلنا : قد مر جوابه ) وهو أن الآية متروكة الظاهر وإلا لزم كون كل مجرم مكذباً القيامة وهو باطل قطعاً. السادس عشر قوله تعالى : وسيق الذين كفروا ﴾ [ الزمر : ٧١] إلى قوله وسيق الذين اتقوا [ الزمر : ۷۳] إذ يعلم منه أن الإنسان إما متق يساق إلى الجنة أو كافر يساق إلى النار (و) الجواب عنه : (قد مر مثله)، وهو أن ذكر قسمين لا يدل على عدم قسم ثالث . ( السابع عشر : قوله عليه السلام من ترك صلاة متعمداً فقد كفر) وقوله عليه السلام : من مات ولم يحج فليمت إن شاء يهودياً وإن شاء نصرانياً قلنا : الآحاد لا تعارض الإجماع المنعقد قبل حدوث المخالفين والثامن عشر ولاية الله وعداوته ضدان فلا واسطة بينهما وولاية الله إيمان وعداوته كفر، قلنا : لا نسلم عدم بين كل ضدين) فإن السواد والبياض متضادان وبينهما واسطة فجاز أن يكون بين ولايته وعداوته واسطة
The fourteenth: His saying, exalted be He: 'But as for those who defiantly disobeyed (fasaqū), their refuge is the Fire' [as-Sajdah 32:20] – the verse, and its completion: 'Every time they wish to emerge from it, they are returned to it, and it is said to them, "Taste the punishment of the Fire which you used to deny."' [32:20]. Indeed, it indicates that every sinner (fāsiq) is a disbeliever. We said: His saying: 'But as for those who defiantly disobeyed' [32:20] is not remaining on its apparent generality because it would require that every sinner denies the Resurrection, and that is definitively false. The fifteenth: His saying, exalted be He: 'They will ask one another about the criminals, "What put you into Saqar?"' [al-Muddaththir 74:40-42] up to His saying: 'And we used to deny the Day of Judgment.' [74:46] So it is established by that that every criminal entering the Fire is a disbeliever, and there is no doubt that the sinner is a criminal [who enters the Fire]. We said: Its answer has already passed: the verse is abandoned in its apparent meaning, otherwise it would require that every criminal denies the Resurrection, and that is definitively false. The sixteenth: His saying, exalted be He: 'And those who disbelieved will be driven' [az-Zumar 39:71] up to His saying: 'And those who feared their Lord will be led' [39:73]. For it is known from it that a person is either a righteous person (muttaqī) led to Paradise or a disbeliever led to the Fire. The answer to it has already passed similarly: the mention of two groups does not indicate the absence of a third group. The seventeenth: His saying, peace be upon him: 'Whoever intentionally leaves a prayer has disbelieved,' and his saying, peace be upon him: 'Whoever dies without performing Hajj, let him die as a Jew if he wishes or as a Christian if he wishes.' We said: Isolated reports (āḥād) do not contradict the consensus (ijmāʿ) that was established before the emergence of dissenters. The eighteenth: The friendship (wilāyah) of God and His enmity (ʿadāwah) are two opposites, so there is no intermediate state between them; and the friendship of God is faith and His enmity is disbelief. We said: We do not concede that there is no intermediate state between every pair of opposites. For black and white are opposites and there is an intermediate between them. So it is possible that there is an intermediate between His friendship and His enmity.
Source pages p. 368

Commentary
This passage presents five concise objections and responses (the fourteenth through eighteenth). The pattern is similar: each proof from revelation or tradition is refuted by showing that its apparent meaning leads to an absurd consequence or that it is not general. The fourteenth proof from Quran 32:20 (about sinners entering the Fire and being told it is because they used to deny) is refuted by noting that it would require every sinner to deny the Resurrection, which is false. The fifteenth from Quran 74:40-46 makes a similar argument about criminals, and the response is the same: the verse's apparent meaning is abandoned. The sixteenth from Quran 39:71-73 divides people into two groups (believers and disbelievers), but the response says mentioning two groups does not preclude a third. The seventeenth uses two hadiths (one about leaving prayer, one about dying without Hajj), and the response says isolated reports (āḥād) cannot override the consensus that existed before these reports emerged. The eighteenth argues that God's friendship and enmity are opposites with no middle ground, but the response gives the counterexample of black and white, which have intermediate colors, so there can be an intermediate state—faith-disobedience without being a disbeliever. These responses demonstrate the Ashʿarī method of defending the possibility of a third category (the fāsiq) between faith and disbelief.

Key Terms
مكذب بالقيامة
متروك الظاهر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: A verse that threatens sinners with eternal punishment must apply to all sinners, including Muslims who commit major sins.
Correction: If taken literally, it would imply all sinners deny Resurrection, which is false; therefore the verse applies only to disbelieving sinners.

Checkpoint
Why does Sanusi reject the apparent meaning of Quran 32:20?
A) Because the verse is abrogated.
B) Because it would require every sinner to deny the Resurrection, which is false.
C) Because the verse only refers to polytheists.
D) Because the verse is metaphorical.

Key Takeaway
A scriptural text's apparent generality can be abandoned if it leads to an absurd consequence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever insisted on a literal interpretation of a Quranic verse that, upon honest reflection, leads to an absurd or contradictory conclusion? What would it cost you to humbly accept the interpretation of the scholars who restrict its meaning? Will you do that today?
?
This lesson shows that a threatening verse like 'their refuge is the Fire' is not always meant as a blanket condemnation. How does this affect your view of God's mercy? Are you willing to stop using fear of literal punishment as your primary motivation, and instead seek to understand the conditions and context? What concrete step will you take to trust God's justice more deeply?
?
Sanusi uses reason to restrict the apparent meaning of a revealed text. Do you trust your intellect when it conflicts with a surface-level reading of scripture? Where in your life do you need to apply this principle—letting reason guide you away from a literal reading that leads to falsehood—and what change in your heart does this demand?
